### What went wrong?

When drag-n-dropping files on a MudFileUpload with custom content, only the ondragenter event fires. Ondragleave does not. Dragging a file over the dropzone fires ondragenter. Dragging the file away from the drop zone again does not fire ondragleave

https://try.mudblazor.com/snippet/cumKOIvUTbEJffRp

1. Open file upload sample in the MudBlazor docs, at the Create a Custom Solution section. I also created a snippet for it which is a copy-paste of the example.

3. Continue dragging the file out of the dropzone again and note the formatting does not switch back.
4. Compare this behaviour to the Using Built-In Controls section, where the formatting returns to normal once the dragged file leaves the drop zone.

v9.3.0

    17	    /// <summary>
    18	    /// A form component that lets users upload one or more files.

    37	            using var registerScope = CreateRegisterScope();

    39	                .WithParameter(() => Files)

    41	            _draggingState = registerScope.RegisterParameter<bool>(nameof(Dragging))

    44	        }

   219	        public long? MaxFileSize { get; set; }
   220

   231	        [CascadingParameter(Name = "ParentDisabled")]

   236	
   237	        /// <summary>
   238	        /// Returns the filenames for the selected files.
   239	        /// </summary>
   240	        /// <remarks>
   241	        /// When <c>T</c> is <see cref="IBrowserFile" />, a single filename is returned.<br />
   242	        /// When <c>T</c> is <see cref="IReadOnlyList{IBrowserFile}">IReadOnlyList&lt;IBrowserFile&gt;</see>, multiple filenames are returned.
   243	        /// </remarks>
   244	        public IReadOnlyList<string> GetFilenames()
   245	        {
   246	            if (EqualityComparer<T>.Default.Equals(_filesState.Value, default))
   247	            {
   248	                return [];
   249	            }
   250	            return _filesState.Value switch
   251	            {
   252	                IBrowserFile singleFile => [singleFile.Name],
   253	                IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile> fileList => fileList.Select(f => f.Name).ToList(),
   254	                _ => []
   255	            };
   256	        }
   257	
   258	        protected bool GetDisabledState() => Disabled || ParentDisabled || ParentReadOnly;
   259	
   260	        private async Task OnDragResetAsync()
   261	        {
   262	            await _draggingState.SetValueAsync(false);
   263	        }
   264	
   265	        private Task OnDragAreaClickAsync()
   266	        {
   267	            if (GetDisabledState())
   268	            {
   269	                return Task.CompletedTask;
   270	            }
   271	
   272	            return OpenFilePickerAsync();
   273	        }
   274	
   275	        private Task OnDragEnterAsync()
   276	        {
   277	            if (GetDisabledState())
   278	            {
   279	                return Task.CompletedTask;
   280	            }
   281	
   282	            return _draggingState.SetValueAsync(true);
   283	        }
   284	
   285	        private Task OnFileChipCloseAsync(string filename)
   286	        {
   287	            if (GetDisabledState())
   288	            {
   289	                return Task.CompletedTask;
   290	            }
   291	
   292	            return RemoveFileAsync(filename);
   293	        }
   294	
   295	        private int _numberOfActiveFileInputs = 1;
   296	        private string? GetInputClass(int fileInputIndex) => fileInputIndex == _numberOfActiveFileInputs
   297	            ? InputClasses
   298	            : $"{InputClasses} d-none";
   299	        private string GetInputId(int fileInputIndex) => $"{_id}-{fileInputIndex}";
   300	        private string GetActiveInputId() => $"{_id}-{_numberOfActiveFileInputs}";
   301	
   302	        /// <summary>
   303	        /// Removes all files with the specified name from <see cref="Files"/>.
   304	        /// </summary>
   305	        /// <param name="filename">The name of the file(s) to remove.</param>
   306	        /// <returns>
   307	        /// <c>true</c> if one or more files were removed; otherwise, <c>false</c>
   308	        /// if no file with the specified name exists in the current selection.
   309	        /// </returns>
   310	        public async Task<bool> RemoveFileAsync(string filename)
   311	        {
   312	            if (string.IsNullOrWhiteSpace(filename))
   313	            {
   314	                Logger.LogWarning("Attempted to remove a file with an invalid filename.");
   315	                return false;
   316	            }
   317	
   318	            var current = _filesState.Value;
   319	
   320	            switch (current)
   321	            {
   322	                case IBrowserFile singleFile when singleFile.Name == filename:
   323	                    // Single selection with matching name: clear selection
   324	                    await _filesState.SetValueAsync(default);
   325	                    return true;
   326	
   327	                case IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile> fileList:
   328	                    {
   329	                        var updatedList = fileList.Where(f => f.Name != filename).ToList();
   330	                        if (updatedList.Count == fileList.Count)
   331	                        {
   332	                            Logger.LogDebug("File '{Filename}' not found in the current selection.", filename);
   333	                            return false;
   334	                        }
   335	
   336	                        if (updatedList.Count == 0)
   337	                        {
   338	                            // Treat removal of the last file as "no selection"
   339	                            await _filesState.SetValueAsync(default);
   340	                        }
   341	                        else
   342	                        {
   343	                            // T is expected to be IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile> here
   344	                            await _filesState.SetValueAsync((T)(object)updatedList);
   345	                        }
   346	
   347	                        return true;
   348	                    }
   349	
   350	                case null:
   351	                    Logger.LogDebug("No files are currently selected.");
   352	                    return false;
   353	
   354	                default:
   355	                    Logger.LogWarning(
   356	                        "File removal by name is not supported for the current files type '{Type}'.",
   357	                        current.GetType().FullName);
   358	                    return false;
   359	            }
   360	        }
   361	
   362	        /// <summary>
   363	        /// Removes the specified file instance from <see cref="Files"/>.
   364	        /// </summary>
   365	        /// <param name="file">The file instance to remove.</param>
   366	        /// <returns>
   367	        /// <c>true</c> if the specified file instance was removed; otherwise, <c>false</c>.
   368	        /// </returns>
   369	        public async Task<bool> RemoveFileAsync(IBrowserFile file)
   370	        {
   371	            if (file is null)
   372	            {
   373	                Logger.LogWarning("Attempted to remove a null file.");
   374	                return false;
   375	            }
   376	
   377	            var current = _filesState.Value;
   378	
   379	            switch (current)
   380	            {
   381	                case IBrowserFile singleFile when ReferenceEquals(singleFile, file):
   382	                    // Single selection with the same instance: clear selection
   383	                    await _filesState.SetValueAsync(default);
   384	                    return true;
   385	
   386	                case IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile> fileList:
   387	                    {
   388	                        // Remove this specific instance (reference-based via List.Remove)
   389	                        var updatedList = fileList.ToList();
   390	                        if (!updatedList.Remove(file))
   391	                        {
   392	                            Logger.LogDebug("The specified file instance was not found in the current selection.");
   393	                            return false;
   394	                        }
   395	
   396	                        if (updatedList.Count == 0)
   397	                        {
   398	                            await _filesState.SetValueAsync(default);
   399	                        }
   400	                        else
   401	                        {
   402	                            await _filesState.SetValueAsync((T)(object)updatedList);
   403	                        }
   404	
   405	                        return true;
   406	                    }
   407	
   408	                case null:
   409	                    Logger.LogDebug("No files are currently selected.");
   410	                    return false;
   411	
   412	                default:
   413	                    Logger.LogWarning(
   414	                        "File removal by instance is not supported for the current files type '{Type}'.",
   415	                        current.GetType().FullName);
   416	                    return false;
   417	            }
   418	        }
   419	
   420	
   421	        /// <summary>
   422	        /// Clears the selected files and resets the internal file inputs.
   423	        /// </summary>
   424	        /// <remarks>
   425	        /// This also removes validation errors produced by file size checks.
   426	        /// </remarks>
   427	        public async Task ClearAsync()
   428	        {
   429	            ValidationErrors.RemoveAll(_validationErrors.Contains);
   430	
   431	            _validationErrors.Clear();
   432	            _numberOfActiveFileInputs = 1;
   433	
   434	            await NotifyValueChangedAsync(default);
   435	            await JsRuntime.InvokeVoidAsyncWithErrorHandling("mudInput.resetValue", GetActiveInputId());
   436	        }
   437	
   438	        /// <summary>
   439	        /// Opens the native file picker for the active input.
   440	        /// </summary>
   441	        public async Task OpenFilePickerAsync()
   442	            => await JsRuntime.InvokeVoidAsyncWithErrorHandling("mudFileUpload.openFilePicker", GetActiveInputId());
   443	
   444	        private async Task OnChangeAsync(InputFileChangeEventArgs args)
   445	        {
   446	            _numberOfActiveFileInputs++;
   447	
   448	            if (GetDisabledState())
   449	                return;
   450	
   451	            await ProcessFileChangeAsync(args);
   452	        }
   453	
   454	        private async Task ProcessFileChangeAsync(InputFileChangeEventArgs args)
   455	        {
   456	            T? value;
   457	
   458	            if (args.FileCount > MaximumFileCount)
   459	            {
   460	                // Notify the consumer about the exceeded file count
   461	                _validationErrors.Add(Localizer[LanguageResource.MudFileUpload_MaximumFileCountExceeded, args.FileCount, MaximumFileCount]);
   462	                await NotifyValueChangedAsync(default); // Reset the value to indicate no valid files were processed
   463	                return;
   464	            }
   465	
   466	            if (typeof(T) == typeof(IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile>))
   467	            {
   468	                value = (T?)(object)ProcessMultipleFiles(args.GetMultipleFiles(MaximumFileCount));
   469	            }
   470	            else if (typeof(T) == typeof(IBrowserFile))
   471	            {
   472	                value = (T?)ProcessSingleFile(args.FileCount == 1 ? args.File : null);
   473	            }
   474	            else
   475	            {
   476	                return;
   477	            }
   478	
   479	            await NotifyValueChangedAsync(value);
   480	
   481	            if (!ErrorState.Value || !SuppressOnChangeWhenInvalid)
   482	                await OnFilesChanged.InvokeAsync(args);
   483	        }
   484	
   485	        private IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile> ProcessMultipleFiles(IReadOnlyCollection<IBrowserFile> files)
   486	        {
   487	            var validFiles = new List<IBrowserFile>();
   488	
   489	            foreach (var file in files)
   490	            {
   491	                if (MaxFileSize.HasValue && file.Size > MaxFileSize.Value)
   492	                {
   493	                    _validationErrors.Add(Localizer[LanguageResource.MudFileUpload_FileSizeError, file.Name, MaxFileSize.Value.ToString()]);
   494	                }
   495	                else
   496	                {
   497	                    validFiles.Add(file);
   498	                }
   499	            }
   500	
   501	            var newFiles = validFiles.AsReadOnly();
   502	
   503	            if (AppendMultipleFiles && _filesState.Value is IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile> oldFiles)
   504	                return oldFiles.Concat(newFiles).ToList().AsReadOnly();
   505	
   506	            return newFiles;
   507	        }
   508	
   509	        private IBrowserFile? ProcessSingleFile(IBrowserFile? file)
   510	        {
   511	            if (file == null)
   512	                return null;
   513	
   514	            if (MaxFileSize.HasValue && file.Size > MaxFileSize.Value)
   515	            {
   516	                _validationErrors.Add(Localizer[LanguageResource.MudFileUpload_FileSizeError, file.Name, MaxFileSize.Value.ToString()]);
   517	                return null;
   518	            }
   519	
   520	            return file;
   521	        }
   522	
   523	        protected override void OnInitialized()
   524	        {
   525	            if (!(typeof(T) == typeof(IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile>) || typeof(T) == typeof(IBrowserFile)))
   526	            {
   527	                Logger.LogWarning("T must be of type {type1} or {type2}", typeof(IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile>), typeof(IBrowserFile));
   528	            }
   529	
   530	            base.OnInitialized();
   531	        }
   532	
   533	        private async Task NotifyValueChangedAsync(T? value)
   534	        {
   535	            Touched = true;
   536	            await _filesState.SetValueAsync(value);
   537	            await BeginValidateAsync();
   538	            FieldChanged(value);
   539	        }
   540	
   541	        /// <inheritdoc />
   542	        protected override IConverter<T?, string?> GetDefaultConverter()
   543	        {
   544	            return new DefaultConverter<T>
   545	            {
   546	                Culture = GetCulture,
   547	                Format = GetFormat
   548	            };
   549	        }
   550	
   551	        protected internal override T? ReadValue => _filesState.Value;
   552	
   553	        protected override Task SetValueCoreAsync(T? value) => _filesState.SetValueAsync(value);
   554	
   555	        protected override async Task ValidateValue()
   556	        {
   557	            await base.ValidateValue();
   558	
   559	            ValidationErrors = [.. ValidationErrors, .. _validationErrors];
   560	            await ErrorState.SetValueAsync(ValidationErrors.Count > 0);
   561	            await ErrorTextState.SetValueAsync(ValidationErrors.FirstOrDefault());
   562	        }
   563	
   564	        /// <inheritdoc />
   565	        public override Task ResetValidationAsync()
   566	        {
   567	            _validationErrors.Clear();
   568	
   569	            return base.ResetValidationAsync();
   570	        }
   571	    }
   572	}

    26	                                     CloseIcon="@Icons.Material.Outlined.Close"
    27	                                     OnClose="@(async () => await context.RemoveFileAsync(file))"
    28	                                     tabindex="-1" />
    29	                        }
    30	                    </div>
    31	                    <MudToolBar Gutters="false"
    32	                                Class="d-flex justify-end align-end gap-4">
    33	                        <MudButton Color="Color.Primary"
    34	                                   OnClick="@context.OpenFilePickerAsync"
    35	                                   Variant="Variant.Filled">
    36	                            Browse files
    37	                        </MudButton>
    38	                        <MudButton Color="Color.Error"
    39	                                   Disabled="@(!context.GetFilenames().Any())"
    40	                                   OnClick="@context.ClearAsync"
    41	                                   Variant="Variant.Filled">
    42	                            Clear
    43	                        </MudButton>
    44	                    </MudToolBar>
    45	                </MudPaper>
    46	            </CustomContent>
    47	            <SelectedTemplate />
    48	        </MudFileUpload>
    49	    </MudCardContent>
    50	</MudCard>
    51	
    52	@code
    53	{
    54	    private const string DefaultDragClass = "relative d-flex flex-column p-r gap-2 rounded-lg border-2 border-dashed pa-4 mt-4 mud-width-full mud-height-full";
    55	    private IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile> _browserFiles =
    56	    [
    57	        new DummyBrowserFile("test1.jpg", DateTimeOffset.Now, 1024, "image/jpeg", []),
    58	        new DummyBrowserFile("test2.jpg", DateTimeOffset.Now, 1024, "image/jpeg", []),
    59	    ];
    60	    private string _dragClass = DefaultDragClass;
    61	    private bool _dragging = false;
    62	
    63	    private void SetDragClass()
    64	    {
    65	        _dragClass = $"{DefaultDragClass} mud-border-success";
    66	        _dragging = true;
    67	    }
    68	
    69	    private void ClearDragClass()
    70	    {
    71	        if (!_dragging)
    72	        {
    73	            _dragClass = DefaultDragClass;
    74	        }
    75	    }
    76	
    77	    public class DummyBrowserFile : IBrowserFile
    78	    {
    79	        public string Name { get; }
    80	        public DateTimeOffset LastModified { get; }
    81	        public long Size { get; }
    82	        public string ContentType { get; }
    83	        public byte[] Content { get; }
    84	
    85	        public DummyBrowserFile(string name, DateTimeOffset lastModified, long size, string contentType, byte[] content)
    86	        {
    87	            Name = name;
    88	            LastModified = lastModified;
    89	            Size = size;
    90	            ContentType = contentType;
    91	            Content = content;
    92	        }
    93	
    94	        public Stream OpenReadStream(long maxAllowedSize = 512000, CancellationToken cancellationToken = default) => new MemoryStream(Content);
    95	    }
    96	}

    34	                </MudText>
    35	                @foreach (var file in _fileNames)
    36	                {
    37	                    <MudChip T="string"
    38	                             Color="Color.Dark"
    39	                             Text="@file"
    40	                             tabindex="-1" />
    41	                }
    42	            </MudPaper>
    43	        </CustomContent>
    44	    </MudFileUpload>
    45	    <MudToolBar Gutters="@false"
    46	                Class="relative d-flex justify-end gap-4">
    47	        <MudButton Color="Color.Primary"

    49	                   Variant="Variant.Filled">
    50	            Browse files
    51	        </MudButton>
    52	        <MudButton Color="Color.Primary"
    53	                   Disabled="@(!_fileNames.Any())"
    54	                   OnClick="@Upload"
    55	                   Variant="Variant.Filled">
    56	            Upload
    57	        </MudButton>
    58	        <MudButton Color="Color.Error"
    59	                   Disabled="@(!_fileNames.Any())"
    60	                   OnClick="@ClearAsync"
    61	                   Variant="Variant.Filled">
    62	            Clear
    63	        </MudButton>
    64	    </MudToolBar>

    66	
    67	@code
    68	{
    69	#nullable enable
    70	    private const string DefaultDragClass = "relative rounded-lg border-2 border-dashed pa-4 mt-4 mud-width-full mud-height-full";
    71	    private readonly List<string> _fileNames = new();
    72	    private string _dragClass = DefaultDragClass;
    73	    private MudFileUpload<IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile>>? _fileUpload;
    74	
    75	    private async Task ClearAsync()
    76	    {
    77	        await (_fileUpload?.ClearAsync() ?? Task.CompletedTask);
    78	        _fileNames.Clear();
    79	        ClearDragClass();
    80	    }
    81	
    82	    private Task OpenFilePickerAsync()
    83	        => _fileUpload?.OpenFilePickerAsync() ?? Task.CompletedTask;
    84	
    85	    private void OnInputFileChanged(InputFileChangeEventArgs e)
    86	    {
    87	        ClearDragClass();
    88	        var files = e.GetMultipleFiles();
    89	        foreach (var file in files)
    90	        {
    91	            _fileNames.Add(file.Name);
    92	        }
    93	    }
    94	
    95	    private void Upload()
    96	    {
    97	        // Upload the files here
    98	        Snackbar.Configuration.PositionClass = Defaults.Classes.Position.TopCenter;
    99	        Snackbar.Add("Upload started (demo).");
   100	    }
   101	
   102	    private void SetDragClass()
   103	        => _dragClass = $"{DefaultDragClass} mud-border-primary";
   104	
   105	    private void ClearDragClass()
   106	        => _dragClass = DefaultDragClass;
   107	}

   218	        {
   219	            InputFileContent[] fileContent =
   220	            [
   221	                InputFileContent.CreateFromText("Garderoben is a farmer!", "upload.txt"),
   222	                InputFileContent.CreateFromText("A Balrog, servant of Morgoth", "upload2.txt")
   223	            ];
   224	
   225	            Thread.CurrentThread.CurrentCulture = CultureInfo.InvariantCulture; //<<< rework this!
   226	            Thread.CurrentThread.CurrentUICulture = CultureInfo.InvariantCulture;
   227	
   228	            var comp = Context.Render<FileUploadFormValidationTest>();
   229	
   230	            var form = comp.Instance.Form;
   231	            await comp.InvokeAsync(() => form.ValidateAsync());
   232	
   233	            form.IsValid.Should().BeFalse(); //form is invalid to start
   234	
   235	            var single = comp.FindComponent<MudFileUpload<IBrowserFile>>();
   236	            single.Instance.GetState(x => x.ErrorText).Should().Be("'File' must not be empty.");
   237	            single.Markup.Should().Contain("'File' must not be empty.");
   238	
   239	            var multiple = comp.FindComponent<MudFileUpload<IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile>>>();
   240	            multiple.Instance.GetState(x => x.ErrorText).Should().Be("'Files' must not be empty.");
   241	            multiple.Markup.Should().Contain("'Files' must not be empty.");
   242	
   243	            var singleInput = single.FindComponent<InputFile>();
   244	            singleInput.UploadFiles(fileContent[0]); //upload first file
   245	
   246	            await comp.InvokeAsync(() => form.ValidateAsync());
   247	
   248	            single.Instance.GetState(x => x.ErrorText).Should().BeNull();
   249	            single.Markup.Should().NotContain("'File' must not be empty.");
   250	
   251	            form.IsValid.Should().BeFalse(); //form is still invalid
   252	
   253	            var multipleInput = multiple.FindComponent<InputFile>();
   254	            multipleInput.UploadFiles(fileContent); //upload second files
   255	
   256	            await comp.InvokeAsync(() => form.ValidateAsync());
   257	
   258	            single.Instance.GetState(x => x.ErrorText).Should().BeNull();
   259	            single.Markup.Should().NotContain("'Files' must not be empty.");
   260	
   261	            form.IsValid.Should().BeTrue(); //form is now valid
   262	        }

   276	            files.Count.Should().Be(11); //ensure there are 11 files
   277	
   278	            var comp = Context.Render<FileUploadMultipleFilesTest>();
   279	
   280	            var multiple = comp.FindComponent<MudFileUpload<IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile>>>();
   281	            var multipleInput = multiple.FindComponent<InputFile>();
   282	            multipleInput.UploadFiles([.. files]); //upload second files
   283	
   284	            comp.Instance.Files.Count.Should()
   285	                .Be(11); //if no error occurs, we have successfully uploaded more than 10 files
   286	        }

   309	        /// </summary>
   310	        [Test]
   311	        [TestCase(true)]
   312	        [TestCase(false)]
   313	        public void FileUploadAppendMultiple(bool appendMultiple)
   314	        {
   315	            var comp = Context.Render<FileUploadAppendMultipleTest>(p =>
   316	                p.Add(x => x.AppendMultipleFiles, appendMultiple));
   317	
   318	            var input = comp.FindComponent<InputFile>();
   319	            input.UploadFiles(GenerateFile(), GenerateFile(), GenerateFile()); //upload first file
   320	            comp.Instance.Files.Count.Should().Be(3);
   321	
   322	            input.UploadFiles(GenerateFile());
   323	            comp.Instance.Files.Count.Should().Be(appendMultiple ? 4 : 1);

   326	            {
   327	                return InputFileContent.CreateFromText("snakex64 is Canadian", $"{Guid.NewGuid()}.txt");

   374	        /// <summary>
   375	        /// FileUpload should generate new InputFile on file change.
   376	        /// </summary>
   377	        [Test]
   378	        public async Task Generate_new_InputFile_on_file_change()
   379	        {
   380	            var comp = Context.Render<MudFileUpload<IBrowserFile>>();
   381	
   382	            // only 1 input element should be present
   383	            comp.FindAll("input").Should().HaveCount(1);
   384	
   385	            // trigger an OnChange on the internal InputFile
   386	            var defaultFile = new DummyBrowserFile("filename.jpg", DateTimeOffset.Now, 0, "image/jpeg", []);
   387	            await comp.InvokeAsync(() => comp.FindComponent<InputFile>().Instance.OnChange.InvokeAsync(new InputFileChangeEventArgs([defaultFile])));
   388	
   389	            // 2 input elements should now be present
   390	            // one should be visible
   391	            comp.FindAll("input:not(.d-none)").Should().HaveCount(1);
   392	            // and the other should no longer be visible
   393	            comp.FindAll("input.d-none").Should().HaveCount(1);
   394	        }

   396	        /// <summary>
   397	        /// FileUpload should trigger the FilesChanged and OnFilesChanged callbacks when appropriate.
   398	        /// </summary>
   399	        [Test]
   400	        public async Task Should_trigger_file_change_callbacks_as_expected()
   401	        {
   402	            var comp = Context.Render<FileUploadChangeCountTests>();
   403	
   404	            // first file change should trigger both callbacks
   405	            var fileContent = new byte[5];
   406	            // fill file content with random bytes
   407	            new Random().NextBytes(fileContent);
   408	            var firstFile = new DummyBrowserFile("filename.jpg", DateTimeOffset.Now, 0, "image/jpeg", fileContent);
   409	            await comp.InvokeAsync(() => comp.FindComponents<InputFile>()[0].Instance.OnChange.InvokeAsync(new InputFileChangeEventArgs([firstFile])));
   410	
   411	            comp.Instance.FilesChangedCount.Should().Be(1);
   412	            comp.Instance.OnFilesChangedCount.Should().Be(1);
   413	
   414	            // since a new InputFile is generated with each upload, we can get the last InputFile in the render chain to emulate a new upload
   415	            // so when a new file reference is uploaded, both file change callbacks should be triggered
   416	            new Random().NextBytes(fileContent);
   417	            var secondFile = new DummyBrowserFile("filename.jpg", DateTimeOffset.Now, 0, "image/jpeg", fileContent);
   418	            await comp.InvokeAsync(() => comp.FindComponents<InputFile>()[^1].Instance.OnChange.InvokeAsync(new InputFileChangeEventArgs([secondFile])));
   419	
   420	            comp.Instance.FilesChangedCount.Should().Be(2);
   421	            comp.Instance.OnFilesChangedCount.Should().Be(2);
   422	        }

   426	        /// </summary>
   427	        [Test]
   428	        public async Task FileUpload_DragAndDrop_Test()
   429	        {
   430	            var comp = Context.Render<MudFileUpload<IBrowserFile>>(parameters => parameters
   431	                .Add(x => x.DragAndDrop, true));
   432	
   433	            // Verify drag area exists
   434	            comp.Find(".mud-file-upload-dragarea").Should().NotBeNull();
   435	
   436	            // Test drag enter
   437	            await comp.Find(".mud-file-upload-dragarea").DragEnterAsync();
   438	            comp.Find(".mud-file-upload-dragarea").ClassList.Should().Contain("mud-border-primary");
   439	
   440	            // Test drag leave
   441	            await comp.Find("input").DragLeaveAsync();
   442	            comp.Find(".mud-file-upload-dragarea").ClassList.Should().NotContain("mud-border-primary");
   443	
   444	            // Test drag end
   445	            await comp.Find("input").DragEndAsync();
   446	            comp.Find(".mud-file-upload-dragarea").ClassList.Should().NotContain("mud-border-primary");
   447	        }

   491	        /// <summary>
   492	        /// Tests RemoveFileAsync functionality for single file
   493	        /// </summary>
   494	        [Test]
   495	        public async Task FileUpload_RemoveFileAsync_SingleFile_Test()
   496	        {
   497	            var fileName = "test.txt";
   498	            var defaultFile = new DummyBrowserFile(fileName, DateTimeOffset.Now, 0, "text/plain", []);
   499	            var comp = Context.Render<MudFileUpload<IBrowserFile>>(parameters => parameters
   500	                .Add(x => x.Files, defaultFile));
   501	
   502	            // Verify initial state
   503	            comp.Instance.Files.Should().NotBeNull();
   504	            comp.Instance.GetFilenames().Should().ContainSingle(x => x == fileName);
   505	
   506	            // Remove file
   507	            await comp.InvokeAsync(() => comp.Instance.RemoveFileAsync(fileName));
   508	
   509	            // Verify file was removed
   510	            comp.Instance.GetState(x => x.Files).Should().BeNull();
   511	            comp.Instance.GetFilenames().Should().BeEmpty();
   512	        }

   517	        [Test]
   518	        public async Task FileUpload_RemoveFileAsync_MultipleFiles_Test()
   519	        {
   520	            var files = new List<IBrowserFile>
   521	            {
   522	                new DummyBrowserFile("test1.txt", DateTimeOffset.Now, 0, "text/plain", []),
   523	                new DummyBrowserFile("test2.txt", DateTimeOffset.Now, 0, "text/plain", [])
   524	            };
   525	
   526	            var comp = Context.Render<MudFileUpload<IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile>>>(parameters => parameters
   527	                .Add(x => x.Files, files));
   528	
   529	            // Verify initial state
   530	            comp.Instance.Files.Should().HaveCount(2);
   531	            comp.Instance.GetFilenames().Should().HaveCount(2);
   532	
   533	            // Remove one file
   534	            await comp.InvokeAsync(() => comp.Instance.RemoveFileAsync("test1.txt"));
   535	
   536	            // Verify file was removed
   537	            comp.Instance.GetState(x => x.Files).Should().HaveCount(1);
   538	            comp.Instance.GetFilenames().Should().ContainSingle(x => x == "test2.txt");
   539	        }

   541	        /// <summary>
   542	        /// Tests SelectedTemplate rendering
   543	        /// </summary>
   544	        [Test]
   545	        public async Task FileUpload_SelectedTemplate_Test()
   546	        {
   547	            // Arrange
   548	            var files = new List<IBrowserFile>
   549	            {
   550	                new DummyBrowserFile("test1.txt", DateTimeOffset.Now, 0, "text/plain", []),
   551	                new DummyBrowserFile("test2.txt", DateTimeOffset.Now, 0, "text/plain", [])
   552	            };
   553	
   554	            // Create the component with initial template
   555	            var comp = Context.Render<MudFileUpload<IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile>>>(parameters => parameters
   556	                .Add(x => x.SelectedTemplate, context => builder =>
   557	                {
   558	                    builder.AddContent(0, $"Selected files: {context?.Count ?? 0}");
   559	                }));
   560	
   561	            // Initial state should show 0 files
   562	            comp.Markup.Should().Contain("Selected files: 0");
   563	
   564	            // Simulate file upload by triggering OnChange
   565	            var inputFile = comp.FindComponent<InputFile>();
   566	            await comp.InvokeAsync(() => inputFile.Instance.OnChange.InvokeAsync(
   567	                new InputFileChangeEventArgs(files)));
   568	
   569	            // Re-render and verify
   570	            comp.Render();
   571	            comp.Markup.Should().Contain("Selected files: 2");

   574	        /// <summary>
   575	        /// Tests the SuppressOnChangeWhenInvalid behavior in the FileUpload component
   576	        /// </summary>
   577	        [Test]
   578	        public async Task FileUpload_SuppressOnChangeWhenInvalidTest()
   579	        {
   580	            // Arrange
   581	            var suppressOnChangeWhenInvalid = true;
   582	            var files = new List<IBrowserFile>
   583	            {
   584	                new DummyBrowserFile("valid.txt", DateTimeOffset.Now, 1024, "text/plain", []),
   585	                new DummyBrowserFile("invalid.txt", DateTimeOffset.Now, 10485761, "text/plain", [])
   586	            };
   587	
   588	            var comp = Context.Render<FileUploadFormValidationTest>(parameters => parameters
   589	                .Add(p => p.SuppressOnChangeWhenInvalid, suppressOnChangeWhenInvalid));
   590	
   591	            // Act 1: Upload a valid file
   592	            await comp.InvokeAsync(() => comp.FindComponents<InputFile>()[0].Instance.OnChange.InvokeAsync(new InputFileChangeEventArgs([files[0]])));
   593	
   594	            // Assert: The valid file should trigger OnFilesChanged
   595	            comp.Instance.Model.File.Should().NotBeNull();
   596	            comp.Instance.Model.File.Name.Should().Be("valid.txt");
   597	            comp.Instance.OnFilesChangedCount.Should().Be(1);
   598	
   599	            // Act 2: Upload an invalid file
   600	            await comp.InvokeAsync(() => comp.FindComponents<InputFile>()[0].Instance.OnChange.InvokeAsync(new InputFileChangeEventArgs([files[1]])));
   601	
   602	            // Assert: The invalid file should NOT trigger OnFilesChanged
   603	            comp.Instance.Model.File.Should().NotBeNull();
   604	            comp.Instance.Model.File.Name.Should().Be("invalid.txt");
   605	            comp.Instance.OnFilesChangedCount.Should().Be(1);
   606	        }

   608	        [Test]
   609	        [TestCase(typeof(IBrowserFile))]
   610	        [TestCase(typeof(IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile>))]
   611	        [TestCase(null)]
   612	        public void GetFilenames_ShouldNotThrow_ForDifferentTypes(Type type)
   613	        {
   614	            // Act & Assert
   615	            Action action = type switch
   616	            {
   617	                not null when type == typeof(IBrowserFile) => () => Context.Render<MudFileUpload<IBrowserFile>>().Instance.GetFilenames(),
   618	                not null when type == typeof(IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile>) => () => Context.Render<MudFileUpload<IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile>>>().Instance.GetFilenames(),
   619	                _ => () => Context.Render<MudFileUpload<object>>().Instance.GetFilenames()
   620	            };
   621	
   622	            action.Should().NotThrow();
   623	        }

   625	        private static InputFileContent CreateDummyFile(string fileName, long size)
   626	        {
   627	            var content = new byte[size];
   628	            var file = new DummyBrowserFile(fileName, DateTimeOffset.Now, size, "application/octet-stream", content);
   629	
   630	            return InputFileContent.CreateFromBinary(file.Content, file.Name, null, file.ContentType);
   631	        }

   634	        public void MaxFileSize_SingleFile_WithinLimit()
   635	        {
   636	            var comp = Context.Render<FileUploadSingleFileTest>(parameters => parameters.Add(p => p.MaxFileSize, 100L));
   637	
   638	            var file = CreateDummyFile("test.txt", 50);
   639	            var input = comp.FindComponent<InputFile>();
   640	
   641	            input.UploadFiles(file);
   642	
   643	            comp.Instance.File.Should().NotBeNull();
   644	            comp.Instance.File.Name.Should().Be("test.txt");
   645	            comp.Instance.File.Size.Should().Be(50);
   646	        }

   648	        [Test]
   649	        public void MaxFileSize_SingleFile_ExceedsLimit()
   650	        {
   651	            var comp = Context.Render<FileUploadSingleFileTest>(parameters => parameters.Add(p => p.MaxFileSize, 100L));
   652	
   653	            var file = CreateDummyFile("test.txt", 150);
   654	            var input = comp.FindComponent<InputFile>();
   655	            var fileUpload = comp.FindComponent<MudFileUpload<IBrowserFile>>().Instance;
   656	
   657	            input.UploadFiles(file);
   658	
   659	            comp.Instance.File.Should().BeNull(); // File should be rejected
   660	            fileUpload.GetState(x => x.Error).Should().BeTrue();
   661	            fileUpload.GetState(x => x.ErrorText).Should().Be("File 'test.txt' exceeds the maximum allowed size of 100 bytes.");
   662	        }

   722	            fileUpload.GetState(x => x.Error).Should().BeTrue();

   728	        {

   770	        [Test]
   771	        public async Task MaxFileSize_ClearValidationAfterError()
   772	        {
   773	            var comp = Context.Render<FileUploadMultipleFilesTest>(parameters => parameters.Add(p => p.MaxFileSize, 100));
   774	
   775	            var file1 = CreateDummyFile("test1.txt", 200);
   776	            var file2 = CreateDummyFile("test2.txt", 300);
   777	
   778	            var input = comp.FindComponent<InputFile>();
   779	
   780	            input.UploadFiles(file1, file2);
   781	
   782	            // Assert initial error state
   783	            comp.Instance.Files.Should().BeEmpty();
   784	
   785	            var fileUpload = comp.FindComponent<MudFileUpload<IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile>>>().Instance;
   786	
   787	            fileUpload.GetState(x => x.Error).Should().BeTrue();
   788	            fileUpload.GetState(x => x.ErrorText).Should().Be("File 'test1.txt' exceeds the maximum allowed size of 100 bytes.");
   789	
   790	            await comp.InvokeAsync(fileUpload.ClearAsync);
   791	
   792	            // Assert cleared state
   793	            comp.Instance.Files.Should().BeNull();
   794	            fileUpload.GetState(x => x.Error).Should().BeFalse(); // Errors should be cleared
   795	            fileUpload.GetState(x => x.ErrorText).Should().BeNullOrEmpty();
   796	            fileUpload.ValidationErrors.Should().BeEmpty(); // ValidationErrors related to MaxFileSize should be cleared
   797	        }

When you have a hidden `InputFile`, drag events on that hidden element may not fire correctly because the element is hidden. The `@ondragleave` on the `InputFile` should fire when the drag leaves the `InputFile` element. But when using custom content, the custom content div wraps around and the hidden input might be positioned differently.

Wait, let me look at the actual issue more carefully. The `InputFile` has `hidden="@(Hidden && !_draggingState.Value ? "" : null)"`. When `Hidden` is true and `_draggingState` is false, the input is hidden. When the user drags enters, `ondragenter` on the custom content fires (set by user), and they set `Dragging` to true. Then `_draggingState` becomes true, making the input visible. But then when dragging leaves, the `ondragleave` should fire on the `InputFile`...

But wait, there's a subtlety: the `InputFile` itself doesn't have `@ondragenter`. So `_draggingState` never becomes true through the `InputFile`. The `InputFile` only becomes visible if `_draggingState` is already true (set by the user via custom content's `ondragenter`).

The real question is: why does `@ondragleave` on the `InputFile` not fire?

Actually, looking more carefully at the code flow: when the user drags a file over the custom content, the `ondragenter` on the custom content fires (user-defined). The user sets `Dragging = true`. Now the `InputFile` becomes visible (because `!_draggingState.Value` is false, so `hidden` is not applied). But when the user drags away, `ondragleave` on the `InputFile` should fire...

Hmm, let me look at this from another angle. Let me check if there's a known Blazor issue with `ondragleave` on `InputFile`.

Actually, I think I see the issue now. The `InputFile` component in Blazor renders an `<input type="file">` element. The `@ondragleave` event is attached to the `<input>` element. But when the `InputFile` is hidden (via the `hidden` attribute), the drag events don't fire on hidden elements in all browsers.

But more critically, looking at the default (non-custom) case:
- The button has `@ondragenter="OnDragEnterAsync"` (line 38)
- The InputFile has `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"` (line 24)

When the user drags over the button, `ondragenter` fires on the button, making `_draggingState = true`. This makes the InputFile visible. Then when the drag leaves, `ondragleave` fires on the InputFile, resetting `_draggingState = false`.

But when using CustomContent, there's no button with `ondragenter`. The user adds their own `ondragenter` on the custom content. But the `ondragleave` is still only on the InputFile. The InputFile might be hidden initially, and even when made visible, the `ondragleave` event might not fire correctly because the drag is happening over the custom content div, not the InputFile.

Wait, actually, I think the issue might be something else. Let me look at the `InputFile` HTML structure. The `InputFile` renders as an `<input type="file">`. The `@ondragleave` on an `<input type="file">` should fire when the drag leaves that input element. But the input element is typically very small (or hidden), so the drag might never "enter" it, and thus `dragleave` would never fire.

Actually, let me re-read the default behavior test:

```csharp
// Test drag enter
await comp.Find(".mud-file-upload-dragarea").DragEnterAsync();
comp.Find(".mud-file-upload-dragarea").ClassList.Should().Contain("mud-border-primary");

// Test drag leave
await comp.Find("input").DragLeaveAsync();
comp.Find(".mud-file-upload-dragarea").ClassList.Should().NotContain("mud-border-primary");
```

So in the default (non-custom) case, `dragenter` is on the button/dragarea, and `dragleave` is on the input. This works because the dragarea and the input are siblings in the DOM.

But with custom content, the custom content wraps the input, and the input is inside the custom content div. Let me look at the HTML structure:

For custom content:
```html
<div class="mud-file-upload-custom-content">
    <!-- user's custom content -->
    <input type="file" ... />
</div>
```

So the input is INSIDE the custom content div. When you drag over the custom content, you're also dragging over the input (since it's inside). Then when you drag leave, you drag leave from the input... but the input is hidden.

Actually, I think the core issue might be simpler. Let me look at the `InputClasses`:

```csharp
protected string InputClasses =>
    new CssBuilder(InputClass)
        .AddClass("mud-file-upload-dragover", DragAndDrop && (Hidden || CustomContent == null))
        .Build();
```

And the `hidden` attribute on the InputFile:
```
hidden="@(Hidden && !_draggingState.Value ? "" : null)"
```

When `CustomContent` is not null and `DragAndDrop` is true:
- `InputClasses` gets `mud-file-upload-dragover` only if `Hidden` is true (since `CustomContent` is not null, `CustomContent == null` is false, so the condition is `Hidden || false` = `Hidden`)
- The input is hidden when `Hidden && !_dragging`

Now, here's the problem: when the user drags over the custom content area, they set `Dragging = true`. This makes the InputFile visible (not hidden). But then when they drag away, `ondragleave` should fire on the InputFile. However, the InputFile is an `<input type="file">` which is a small element. The dragleave event fires when the mouse leaves the element. But the issue might be that `ondragleave` fires on the input when the drag moves from the input to a child element inside the custom content div. 

Actually wait, `dragleave` events fire when you leave an element AND enter a child element. This is a known issue with HTML5 drag and drop. The `dragleave` event fires when you move from a parent to a child element.

Now I see the pattern. In all the custom content examples, the users are expected to set `@ondragenter` and `@ondragleave` on the component itself (MudFileUpload), and these get passed through to the `InputFile` via `@attributes="UserAttributes"`. Wait, `UserAttributes` - let me check what that is.

Looking at line 22 in the razor file: `@attributes="UserAttributes"`. This means any additional attributes passed to `MudFileUpload` are forwarded to the `InputFile`. So when users write:
```
<MudFileUpload @ondragenter="@SetDragClass"
               @ondragleave="@ClearDragClass" ...>
```

These are passed as additional attributes to the `InputFile`. But wait, the `InputFile` already has:
```
@ondrop="OnDragResetAsync"
@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"
@ondragend="OnDragResetAsync"
```

So `@ondragleave` is set BOTH explicitly AND via `UserAttributes`. In Blazor, when you have duplicate attributes, the explicit one wins (or the later one). Actually, let me think about this more carefully...

In Blazor, `@attributes="UserAttributes"` will spread the attributes. If there's a conflict with an explicitly set attribute, the explicit one takes precedence. So `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"` would override any `ondragleave` from `UserAttributes`.

But wait, that's actually fine because `OnDragResetAsync` sets `_draggingState` to false, and then the user's `DraggingChanged` callback would fire (due to the two-way binding or event callback). Let me re-examine...

Actually, wait. Let me look at the `InputFile` more carefully. The `InputFile` has:
- `@ondrop="OnDragResetAsync"` (line 23)
- `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"` (line 24)
- `@ondragend="OnDragResetAsync"` (line 25)

But it does NOT have `@ondragenter`. So `@ondragenter` from `UserAttributes` would be passed through correctly.

Now the bug: `@ondragleave` does not fire when you drag leave. The `InputFile` has `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"` explicitly, and this should work. But the issue says it doesn't fire.

Wait, I need to re-examine. Let me look at the `hidden` attribute logic:

```
hidden="@(Hidden && !_draggingState.Value ? "" : null)"
```

- When `Hidden` is `true` (default) and `_draggingState` is `false`: the input is hidden
- When `Hidden` is `true` and `_draggingState` is `true`: the input is visible
- When `Hidden` is `false`: the input is always visible

In the custom content scenario from the docs (FileUploadCustomExample.razor):
- `Hidden` is not set, so it defaults to `true`
- `DragAndDrop` is `true`
- The user sets `@ondragenter="@SetDragClass"` on their custom content (MudPaper)
- The user binds `@bind-Dragging="@_dragging"`

When the user drags enters the MudPaper, `SetDragClass` is called which sets `_dragging = true`. This triggers `DraggingChanged`, which updates `_draggingState` to `true`. Now the InputFile becomes visible. 

But then when the drag leaves, the `ondragleave` on the InputFile should fire... but maybe it doesn't because:
1. The InputFile is inside the custom content div
2. The dragleave event might fire incorrectly due to child elements

Actually, I think I found the issue! Let me look at the InputFile's `hidden` attribute again:

```
hidden="@(Hidden && !_draggingState.Value ? "" : null)"
```

When `Hidden` is `true` and `_draggingState` is `false`, the input has `hidden=""` attribute. When the drag starts, `_draggingState` becomes `true`, so the hidden attribute is removed. But the `InputFile` also has this class logic:

```csharp
protected string InputClasses =>
    new CssBuilder(InputClass)
        .AddClass("mud-file-upload-dragover", DragAndDrop && (Hidden || CustomContent == null))
        .Build();

2026-05-29 10:59:56,670 - INFO - swea-agent-MudBlazor__MudBlazor-13063 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I see the issue clearly!

Look at the HTML structure when `CustomContent` is provided:

```html
<MudInputControl>
    <InputContent>
        <!-- InputFile elements (hidden) -->
        <InputFile ... />
        
        <!-- Custom content div -->
        <div class="mud-file-upload-custom-content">
            <!-- user's custom content -->
        </div>
    </InputContent>
</MudInputControl>
```

The `InputFile` elements come BEFORE the custom content div in the DOM. But from the CSS:

```scss
.mud-file-upload-dragover {
    position: absolute;
    width: 100%;
    height: 100%;
    opacity: 0;
    top: 0;
    left: 0;
    z-index: 2;
}
```

The `mud-file-upload-dragover` class makes the input positioned absolutely over the entire area. This class is added when `DragAndDrop && (Hidden || CustomContent == null)`.

So when `CustomContent` is NOT null AND `DragAndDrop` is true AND `Hidden` is true (default):
- `InputClasses` = `"mud-file-upload-dragover"` (since `Hidden` is true)
- The InputFile has `class="mud-file-upload-dragover"` and is positioned absolutely over everything

But the `hidden` attribute on the InputFile: `hidden="@(Hidden && !_draggingState.Value ? "" : null)"`

When the user is NOT dragging (`_draggingState` is false), `Hidden && !false` = `true && true` = the input IS hidden. When the user starts dragging, `_draggingState` becomes true, so `Hidden && !true` = `true && false` = the input is NOT hidden.

Now, the issue: `@ondragenter` is NOT on the `InputFile`. It's only on the button (for non-custom case). So when using custom content, the user must set `@ondragenter` on their custom content. This makes `Dragging` true, which makes the input visible. But then, the `@ondragleave` on the `InputFile` should fire when the drag leaves... 

But wait! There's a key issue: The `InputFile` has `@attributes="UserAttributes"`. If the user sets `@ondragenter` on `MudFileUpload`, that goes into `UserAttributes` and gets passed to `InputFile`. But the `InputFile` already has explicit `@ondragleave`, `@ondrop`, `@ondragend` but NOT `@ondragenter`. So `@ondragenter` from `UserAttributes` would work fine.

But the problem is that the `InputFile` is HIDDEN (has `hidden` attribute) when the user first drags. Drag events don't fire on hidden elements! So `@ondragenter` on the `InputFile` doesn't fire, which means `_draggingState` never becomes true, which means the input stays hidden, which means `@ondragleave` also never fires.

Wait, but the user sets `@ondragenter` on their custom content (the `MudPaper`), not on the `InputFile`. And they set `Dragging` to true manually. So `_draggingState` becomes true, and the input becomes visible. Then `@ondragleave` should fire on the now-visible `InputFile`.

But here's the catch: `dragleave` events are tricky. When you have an absolutely positioned element over other elements, `dragleave` fires when you leave that element. But `dragleave` also fires when you enter a child element of that element. Since the `InputFile` is an `<input type="file">`, it has no children, so that shouldn't be an issue.

However, I think the real problem is that the input, when not hidden, is absolutely positioned over the custom content. When the user drags over the area, `dragenter` fires on the custom content (the `MudPaper`). The user sets `Dragging = true`. Now the input becomes visible and is absolutely positioned on top. The drag is now OVER the input (since it's on top with z-index 2). When the user drags away, `dragleave` should fire on the input...

But wait, the input was hidden before, and when it becomes visible, the drag might not be "over" it yet. Actually, `dragenter` should fire on the input when the input becomes visible under the cursor. Let me think again...

Actually, I think the issue might be simpler. Let me look at the `hidden` attribute behavior. The `hidden` attribute is: `hidden="@(Hidden && !_draggingState.Value ? "" : null)"`. When `Hidden` is true and `_draggingState` is false, the input has `hidden=""`. When `_draggingState` becomes true, the `hidden` attribute is removed.

But here's the thing: in the custom content scenario, the InputFile has `class="mud-file-upload-dragover"` (since `Hidden` is true and `CustomContent` is not null, the condition `Hidden || CustomContent == null` = `true || false` = `true`). This class makes the input absolutely positioned with `opacity: 0`. But the `hidden` attribute also hides it. When `_draggingState` becomes true, the `hidden` is removed, but the input is still `opacity: 0` (from the CSS class). It's still there, just invisible. So drag events should still work.

Hmm, let me look at this from a completely different angle. Let me search for any other recent fixes or issues related to this:

Due to how Blazor handles duplicate attributes, the explicit ones should take precedence over `UserAttributes`. So `@ondragleave` from `UserAttributes` (which is `ClearDragClass`) might be overridden by the explicit `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"`.\n\nActually, in Blazor, when you have both `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"` (explicit) and `@attributes="UserAttributes"` (which contains `ondragleave`), the explicit one wins. So `OnDragResetAsync` is called instead of the user\'s `ClearDragClass`. But `OnDragResetAsync` just sets `_draggingState` to false. However, the user doesn\'t use `@bind-Dragging`, so `DraggingChanged` doesn\'t fire anything... Hmm.\n\nWait, but the user IS setting `@ondragleave` on `MudFileUpload`. Let me look at the example again:\n\n```razor\n<MudFileUpload T="IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile>"\n               @ref="@_fileUpload"\n               OnFilesChanged="OnInputFileChanged"\n               AppendMultipleFiles\n               Hidden="@false"\n               InputClass="file-upload-input"\n               tabindex="-1"\n               @ondrop="@ClearDragClass"\n               @ondragenter="@SetDragClass"\n               @ondragleave="@ClearDragClass"\n               @ondragend="@ClearDragClass">\n```\n\nThese `@ondragenter`, `@ondragleave`, etc. are passed as additional attributes to `MudFileUpload`. Now I have a clearer picture. Let me examine the issue more carefully.

Looking at the examples:

1. **FileUploadDragAndDropCustomScenarioExample.razor** (the "Create a Custom Solution" referenced in the PR):
   - Sets `Hidden="@false"` 
   - Sets `InputClass="file-upload-input"` which has `position: absolute; width: 100%; height: 100%; overflow: hidden; z-index: 10; opacity: 0;`
   - Uses `@ondragenter`, `@ondragleave`, `@ondragend` on `MudFileUpload` directly (which pass to InputFile via UserAttributes)
   - Does NOT use `@bind-Dragging`

2. **FileUploadCustomExample.razor** (another custom example):
   - Uses `@bind-Dragging="@_dragging"`
   - Sets `@ondragenter="@SetDragClass"` on the custom content (MudPaper)
   - Does NOT set `@ondragleave` on anything
   - Relies on `@bind-Dragging:after="@ClearDragClass"` to clear when `Dragging` becomes false

The PR description mentions the snippet `cumKOIvUTbEJffRp` which is a copy-paste of the "Create a Custom Solution" section. Looking at the snippet URL pattern, this would be the `FileUploadDragAndDropCustomScenarioExample.razor` example (or similar).

Now let me re-examine the problem. In `FileUploadDragAndDropCustomScenarioExample.razor`:
- `Hidden="@false"` - the input is NOT hidden
- The input has `InputClass="file-upload-input"` which makes it absolutely positioned with opacity 0
- `@ondragenter`, `@ondragleave`, `@ondragend` are set on `MudFileUpload`, which pass to `InputFile` via `UserAttributes`

But wait, the `InputFile` already has explicit `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"` and `@ondragend="OnDragResetAsync"`. Due to how Blazor handles duplicate attributes, the explicit ones should take precedence over `UserAttributes`. So `@ondragleave` from `UserAttributes` (which is `ClearDragClass`) might be overridden by the explicit `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"`.

Actually, in Blazor, when you have both `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"` (explicit) and `@attributes="UserAttributes"` (which contains `ondragleave`), the explicit one wins. So `OnDragResetAsync` is called instead of the user's `ClearDragClass`. But `OnDragResetAsync` just sets `_draggingState` to false. However, the user doesn't use `@bind-Dragging`, so `DraggingChanged` doesn't fire anything... Hmm.

Wait, but the user IS setting `@ondragleave` on `MudFileUpload`. Let me look at the example again:

```razor
<MudFileUpload T="IReadOnlyList<IBrowserFile>"
               @ref="@_fileUpload"
               OnFilesChanged="OnInputFileChanged"
               AppendMultipleFiles
               Hidden="@false"
               InputClass="file-upload-input"
               tabindex="-1"
               @ondrop="@ClearDragClass"
               @ondragenter="@SetDragClass"
               @ondragleave="@ClearDragClass"
               @ondragend="@ClearDragClass">
```

These `@ondragenter`, `@ondragleave`, etc. are passed as additional attributes to `MudFileUpload`. They go into `UserAttributes` dictionary and are spread onto the `InputFile` via `@attributes="UserAttributes"`.

But the `InputFile` already has `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"` (explicit). In Blazor, the explicit attribute takes precedence, so the `ondragleave` from `UserAttributes` is effectively ignored!

That's the bug! The `@ondragleave` from the user is overridden by the component's own `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"`.

Similarly, `@ondrop` and `@ondragend` are also overridden.

But wait, for the non-custom case (DragAndDrop with the button), this works fine because:
- `@ondragenter` is on the button (calls `OnDragEnterAsync` which sets `_draggingState = true`)
- The InputFile becomes visible
- `@ondragleave` on the InputFile calls `OnDragResetAsync` which sets `_draggingState = false`

But for the custom case, the user expects `@ondragleave` to call their `ClearDragClass` method. However, `OnDragResetAsync` is called instead (which also sets `_draggingState = false`). But the user's `ClearDragClass` never gets called.

But wait, that's not the issue described. The issue says `ondragleave` does NOT fire at all. If `OnDragResetAsync` was being called, `_draggingState` would become false, and the `Dragging` parameter would update. But the user says the formatting does NOT switch back.

Let me re-read the PR description more carefully:

> When drag-n-dropping files on a MudFileUpload with custom content, only the ondragenter event fires. Ondragleave does not. Dragging a file over the dropzone fires ondragenter. Dragging the file away from the drop zone again does not fire ondragleave

So `ondragleave` does not fire at all. Not that it fires the wrong handler, but that it doesn't fire.

The reproduction link points to a snippet that is a copy-paste of the "Create a Custom Solution" example. Let me look at that specific example again:

`FileUploadDragAndDropCustomScenarioExample.razor`:
- `Hidden="@false"` - input is visible
- `InputClass="file-upload-input"` with absolute positioning, opacity 0
- The custom content is a `MudPaper` inside `CustomContent`

The input is visible (not hidden), absolutely positioned over the entire area with opacity 0. It has `@ondragleave` from both the explicit `OnDragResetAsync` and the user's `ClearDragClass` (via UserAttributes). 

Now, why would `ondragleave` not fire? Let me think about the HTML structure:

```html
<MudInputControl>
    <InputContent>  <!-- This is a RenderFragment, rendered as part of the parent -->
        <input type="file" class="file-upload-input" ... />  <!-- absolutely positioned, opacity 0, z-index 10 -->
        <div class="mud-file-upload-custom-content">
            <div class="...">  <!-- user's MudPaper -->
                ...
            </div>
        </div>
    </InputContent>
</MudInputControl>
```

The input is absolutely positioned over the entire area, including the custom content. When the user drags over, `dragenter` fires on the input. When they drag away, `dragleave` should fire on the input.

But wait, there's a subtlety with CSS `display: contents`:

```scss
> .mud-input-control-input-container {
    display: contents;
}

> .mud-input-control-input-container > .mud-file-upload-custom-content {
    display: contents;
}
```

The `display: contents` makes the container effectively disappear from the layout, and its children are treated as if they are direct children of the parent. This could affect event handling.

But actually, I think I need to focus on the actual problem. Let me look at the `FileUploadCustomExample.razor` more closely, which is the example from the docs "Create a Custom Solution" section:

In `FileUploadCustomExample.razor`:
- The user sets `@ondragenter="@SetDragClass"` on the `MudPaper` (custom content)
- The user binds `@bind-Dragging="@_dragging"` with `@bind-Dragging:after="@ClearDragClass"`
- There is NO `@ondragleave` on anything

So when the user drags enters the MudPaper, `SetDragClass` fires, setting `_dragClass` and `_dragging = true`. This triggers `DraggingChanged`, which sets `_draggingState = true`. The InputFile becomes visible (since `hidden` is removed).

But when the user drags away, the `ondragleave` on the InputFile should fire, calling `OnDragResetAsync`, which sets `_draggingState = false`. This triggers `DraggingChanged` which sets `_dragging = false`. Then `ClearDragClass` fires (via `@bind-Dragging:after`).

But the user says this doesn't work. The `ondragleave` doesn't fire.

Wait, I just realized something. Let me check the InputFile's `hidden` attribute condition:

```
hidden="@(Hidden && !_draggingState.Value ? "" : null)"
```

In the `FileUploadCustomExample.razor`:
- `Hidden` is NOT set, so it defaults to `true`
- Initially, `_draggingState` is `false`, so `Hidden && !false` = `true` → the input IS hidden
- When `_draggingState` becomes `true`, `Hidden && !true` = `false` → the input is NOT hidden

But when the input is hidden, does `ondragleave` fire? In most browsers, events don't fire on hidden elements. But the issue says `ondragenter` fires (which makes the input visible), and then `ondragleave` should fire when leaving. But maybe there's a timing issue?

Actually, I think I found the real issue! Let me look at the `InputClasses`:

```csharp
protected string InputClasses =>
    new CssBuilder(InputClass)
        .AddClass("mud-file-upload-dragover", DragAndDrop && (Hidden || CustomContent == null))
        .Build();
```

When `CustomContent` is not null:
- `CustomContent == null` is `false`
- So the condition is `DragAndDrop && Hidden`
- If `Hidden` is true (default), the input gets class `mud-file-upload-dragover`

The CSS for `mud-file-upload-dragover`:
```scss
.mud-file-upload-dragover {
    position: absolute;
    width: 100%;
    height: 100%;
    opacity: 0;
    top: 0;
    left: 0;
    z-index: 2;
}
```

So the input is absolutely positioned but has `opacity: 0`. It's invisible but still receives events.

Now when the input also has the `hidden` attribute (because `Hidden=true` and `!_draggingState` is true), it's hidden AND absolutely positioned. Hidden elements don't receive events.

When `_draggingState` becomes true, the `hidden` attribute is removed, and the input becomes capable of receiving events. But here's the question: does the `dragleave` event fire correctly?

I think the problem might be that when the user drags away from the custom content area, the drag first leaves the input (which is absolutely positioned over everything), firing `dragleave` on the input. But then immediately after, the drag might enter another element, causing a `dragenter` on that element, and so on. The `dragleave` event should fire...

Actually, let me reconsider. I think the issue might be more fundamental. Let me look at what the `InputFile` component actually renders in Blazor. The `InputFile` component renders an `<input type="file">` element. The `@ondragleave` directive adds an event handler for the `dragleave` event.

But here's a key point: `<input type="file">` elements have special rendering in browsers. They typically render as a button with text. The drag events might not work reliably on file inputs because the browser's native file input UI might interfere.

Actually, I think I've been overthinking this. Let me focus on the actual difference between the working case (non-custom) and the broken case (custom).

**Working case (DragAndDrop without CustomContent):**
- The button has `@ondragenter="OnDragEnterAsync"` 
- The InputFile has `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"`
- When drag enters the button → `_draggingState = true` → input visible
- When drag leaves the input → `_draggingState = false`

**Broken case (CustomContent with DragAndDrop):**

- The user sets `@ondragenter` on their custom content
- When drag enters custom content → user's handler fires → user sets `Dragging = true` → `_draggingState = true` → input visible

When using `CustomContent`, the button with `@ondragenter="OnDragEnterAsync"` is not rendered\n\nSo when the user has custom content:\n- The user must set `@ondragenter` on their custom content to set `Dragging = true`\n- This makes `_draggingState = true`, which makes the `InputFile` visible (removes `hidden` attribute)\n- But then, does `@ondragleave` on the `InputFile` fire?\n\nThe issue could be that `@ondragleave` on the `InputFile` IS being overridden by `UserAttributes`. 2026-05-29 11:20:56,485 - INFO - swea-agent-MudBlazor__MudBlazor-13063 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I think I've finally identified the core issue. Let me trace through the scenarios:

**Scenario 1: Default (DragAndDrop=true, no CustomContent)**
- Button has `@ondragenter="OnDragEnterAsync"` → sets `_draggingState = true`
- InputFile has `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"` → sets `_draggingState = false`
- This works because: drag enters button → input becomes visible → drag leaves input → input becomes hidden again

**Scenario 2: CustomContent with DragAndDrop (the bug)**
- There is NO element with `@ondragenter` that sets `_draggingState = true`
- The user must set `@ondragenter` on their own custom content
- But the InputFile ALSO needs to detect dragenter to make itself visible

Wait, but in Scenario 2, the user typically sets up their own dragenter handling. Let me look at how the two main examples differ:

**FileUploadDragAndDropCustomScenarioExample.razor**: Uses `Hidden="@false"` and `InputClass="file-upload-input"` (which has `position: absolute; opacity: 0; z-index: 10`). This makes the input always visible (not hidden) but transparent. The `@ondragenter`, `@ondragleave`, etc. are passed to the InputFile via UserAttributes. This should work because the input is never hidden.

**FileUploadCustomExample.razor**: Uses default `Hidden=true`. The user sets `@ondragenter` on the MudPaper (custom content). The user binds `@bind-Dragging`. This should also work because:
1. Drag enters MudPaper → `SetDragClass` called → `_dragging = true` → `DraggingChanged` → `_draggingState = true`
2. Input becomes visible (hidden removed)
3. Drag leaves → `ondragleave` on InputFile fires → `OnDragResetAsync` → `_draggingState = false` → `DraggingChanged` → `ClearDragClass`

But the user says step 3 doesn't happen. Why?

Let me check: the `InputFile` has `hidden="@(Hidden && !_draggingState.Value ? "" : null)"`. When `Hidden=true` and `_draggingState=true`, the input is NOT hidden. But it also has the CSS class `mud-file-upload-dragover` (because `DragAndDrop && (Hidden || CustomContent == null)` = `true && (true || false)` = `true`). This class makes it `position: absolute; width: 100%; height: 100%; opacity: 0; z-index: 2`.

So the input is:
- Not hidden
- Absolutely positioned over the entire area
- Opacity 0 (invisible but receives events)
- z-index 2

The custom content div has `display: contents` (from CSS `.mud-file-upload-custom-content { display: contents; }`).

Wait, `display: contents` on the custom content div means the div itself is not rendered as a box; its children are treated as if they were direct children of the parent. This is important for event handling.

Now, when the user drags over the area:
1. The input is hidden initially (when not dragging)
2. The user's `@ondragenter` on MudPaper fires → `_draggingState = true` → input becomes visible (not hidden)
3. The input appears on top (z-index 2, absolute positioned)
4. When the user drags away, does `dragleave` fire on the input?

Actually, wait. When the input becomes visible (not hidden), does the drag enter it? The `dragenter` event should fire on the input when it becomes visible under the cursor. But the input is absolutely positioned with opacity 0. It should still receive events.

But here's the key: when the input doesn't have `@ondragenter`, the `dragenter` event on the input doesn't do anything special. The input just becomes visible. Then when the user drags away, `dragleave` should fire.

Unless... the `display: contents` on the parent interferes. When the parent has `display: contents`, the parent is not a box, and events might not propagate correctly.

Actually, I think I may have been overthinking this. Let me look at the actual issue from a different angle. Let me search for any related PRs or commits that might have addressed this:

If the user sets `@ondragleave` on the `MudFileUpload`, it gets passed to `InputFile` via `UserAttributes`. This element might not span the full width/height even with CSS, because the browser's native rendering of file inputs can be tricky.

Now I see the exact pattern that triggers the bug! Look at lines 80-93:

```csharp
private void SetDragClass()
{
    _dragClass = $"{DefaultDragClass} mud-border-primary";
    _dragging = true;
}

private void ClearDragClass()
{
    if (!_dragging)
    {
        _dragClass = DefaultDragClass;
    }
}
```

And the component binding:
```razor
@bind-Dragging="@_dragging"
@bind-Dragging:after="@ClearDragClass"
```

So:
1. `SetDragClass` is called on `@ondragenter` (on the MudPaper). It sets `_dragging = true` and updates the drag class.
2. This triggers `DraggingChanged` (due to `@bind-Dragging`), which sets `_draggingState = true`.
3. When `_draggingState` becomes true, the InputFile becomes visible (hidden is removed).
4. When the user drags away, `@ondragleave` on InputFile should fire `OnDragResetAsync`, which sets `_draggingState = false`.
5. `DraggingChanged` fires, setting `_dragging = false`.
6. `ClearDragClass` is called (via `@bind-Dragging:after`), which checks `if (!_dragging)` - but `_dragging` is now `false`, so `!_dragging` is `true`, and it clears the drag class.

But wait, the issue says step 4 doesn't happen. `ondragleave` doesn't fire on the InputFile.

Let me think about why... 

When the InputFile has `class="mud-file-upload-dragover"`, it's `position: absolute; width: 100%; height: 100%; opacity: 0; z-index: 2`. It's absolutely positioned relative to its nearest positioned ancestor. The parent `.mud-input-control-input-container` has `display: contents`, so it's not a positioning context. The grandparent `.mud-file-upload` might or might not be positioned.

Let me check the CSS more carefully:

```scss
.mud-file-upload {
  flex-grow: 0;

  > .mud-input-control-input-container {
    display: contents;
  }
  ...
}
```

The `.mud-file-upload` doesn't have `position: relative`. So the absolutely positioned input would be positioned relative to the nearest positioned ancestor, which could be something higher up in the DOM. This could cause the input to be positioned incorrectly, potentially outside the visible area, meaning drag events wouldn't reach it.

I think the issue might be with how Blazor handles the `hidden` attribute. In Blazor, `hidden="@(condition ? "" : null)"` - when condition is false, `hidden` is set to `null`, which Blazor renders as no attribute (removes it). When condition is true, `hidden=""` is rendered.

The `dragenter` event fires when the drag first enters the element. If the element wasn\'t there when the drag entered, it won\'t fire. However, `dragover` fires continuously while the drag is over an element. And `dragleave` fires when the drag leaves the element.\n\nBut for `dragleave` to fire, the browser needs to know that the drag was "over" the input. If the input became visible after the drag was already over it, the browser might not consider the drag as being "over" the input, and thus `dragleave` might not fire when the drag moves away.\n\nThis is a timing/state issue. 2026-05-29 11:28:57,643 - INFO - swea-agent-MudBlazor__MudBlazor-13063 - 💭 THOUGHT
OK, I've been analyzing this for a while. Let me now focus on what I believe the fix should be.

The core problem is:

1. The `InputFile` has explicit `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"` which overrides any user-provided `ondragleave` from `UserAttributes`.
2. The `InputFile` does NOT have `@ondragenter`, so when using custom content, the input never detects drag enter on its own. The user must set `@ondragenter` on their custom content. But even when the user does this and makes `_draggingState = true` (through `@bind-Dragging`), the `@ondragleave` on the input might not fire because the input was hidden when the drag started.

Actually, wait. Let me re-read the test:

```csharp
// Test drag enter
await comp.Find(".mud-file-upload-dragarea").DragEnterAsync();
comp.Find(".mud-file-upload-dragarea").ClassList.Should().Contain("mud-border-primary");

// Test drag leave
await comp.Find("input").DragLeaveAsync();
comp.Find(".mud-file-upload-dragarea").ClassList.Should().NotContain("mud-border-primary");
```

This test works. The input was initially hidden, but after `DragEnterAsync` on the button (which sets `_draggingState = true`), the input becomes visible. Then `DragLeaveAsync` on the input works.

So the issue must be something else. Let me look at the test more carefully. In the test, the input is found via `comp.Find("input")`. But when there are multiple inputs (due to `_numberOfActiveFileInputs`), which one is found? Let me check if there could be multiple inputs.

In the test, `_numberOfActiveFileInputs` is 1 (initial state). So there's only one input. The test works.

Now, in the custom content case, the same should happen: `_draggingState` becomes true, input becomes visible, `dragleave` on input should fire.

Unless... the issue is that the user's `@ondragleave` (from `UserAttributes`) is being overridden by the explicit `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"`. The user's handler is never called. But `OnDragResetAsync` IS called, which sets `_draggingState = false`. So the drag state does reset, but the user's handler (which might update CSS classes) doesn't run.

Wait, but in `FileUploadCustomExample.razor`, the user uses `@bind-Dragging` and `@bind-Dragging:after`. When `OnDragResetAsync` sets `_draggingState = false`, `DraggingChanged` fires, which updates `_dragging`, which triggers `ClearDragClass`. So the user's handler SHOULD be called indirectly.

But the PR says it doesn't work. Let me look at `ClearDragClass` in `FileUploadCustomExample.razor`:

```csharp
private void ClearDragClass()
{
    if (!_dragging)
    {
        _dragClass = DefaultDragClass;
    }
}
```

Wait, this checks `if (!_dragging)`. But at this point, `_dragging` has been set to `false` by the binding. So `!_dragging` is `true`, and it clears the drag class. This should work!

But hold on: the `@bind-Dragging:after="@ClearDragClass"` fires AFTER `Dragging` changes. So:
1. `OnDragResetAsync` sets `_draggingState = false`
2. `DraggingChanged` fires
3. `_dragging` is updated to `false` (via two-way binding)
4. `ClearDragClass` is called (via `:after`)
5. `ClearDragClass` checks `if (!_dragging)` → true → clears drag class

This should work! But the user says it doesn't. So maybe `OnDragResetAsync` is never called because `ondragleave` doesn't fire on the InputFile.

Let me think about why `ondragleave` wouldn't fire. What if the InputFile is still hidden when the drag leaves? What if `_draggingState` never becomes true?

In `FileUploadCustomExample.razor`:
- The user sets `@ondragenter="@SetDragClass"` on the `MudPaper` (custom content)
- `SetDragClass` sets `_dragClass = ...` and `_dragging = true`
- `_dragging = true` triggers `DraggingChanged`, which sets `_draggingState = true`
- Now the InputFile should become visible

But wait - there's a subtlety here. The `@bind-Dragging="@_dragging"` means:
- When `_dragging` changes, `Dragging` parameter is updated (and `DraggingChanged` is invoked)
- When `Dragging` parameter changes (via `DraggingChanged`), `_dragging` is updated

So the flow is:
1. User's `SetDragClass` → `_dragging = true`
2. Blazor detects `_dragging` changed → fires `DraggingChanged` event callback
3. `DraggingChanged` → `_draggingState.SetValueAsync(true)` → this triggers a re-render
4. After re-render, `Dragging` parameter is `true`, so `@bind-Dragging` updates `_dragging` to `true` (but it's already `true`)

This should work. The `_draggingState` becomes true, the input becomes visible.

But wait, what if there's an issue with the order of operations? What if `SetDragClass` fires and sets `_dragging = true`, but the re-render happens after the dragleave event would have fired? That seems unlikely.

Let me try a completely different approach. Let me actually write a test that reproduces the issue and run it.

```
hidden="@(Hidden && !_draggingState.Value ? "" : null)"
```

When `Hidden` is true (default) and `_draggingState` is false, the input has `hidden=""` attribute. When a drag starts, `_draggingState` becomes true, so the `hidden` attribute is removed.

But now with my fix, `@ondragenter` is on the InputFile. When the input is hidden, `ondragenter` can't fire (hidden elements don't receive events). So the input stays hidden.
