2026-05-29 11:45:17,958 - INFO - swea-agent-MudBlazor__MudBlazor-13063 - 💭 THOUGHT
Let me now write a quick test to reproduce the issue programmatically and see if my fix helps. But first, let me think about what the actual root cause is.

Let me re-read the PR description once more:

> When drag-n-dropping files on a MudFileUpload with custom content, only the ondragenter event fires. Ondragleave does not. Dragging a file over the dropzone fires ondragenter. Dragging the file away from the drop zone again does not fire ondragleave

> Reproduction steps:
> 1. Open file upload sample in the MudBlazor docs, at the Create a Custom Solution section. I also created a snippet for it which is a copy-paste of the example.
> 2. Drag a file over the dropzone and note the formatting change.
> 3. Continue dragging the file out of the dropzone again and note the formatting does not switch back.
> 4. Compare this behaviour to the Using Built-In Controls section, where the formatting returns to normal once the dragged file leaves the drop zone.

The "Create a Custom Solution" section in the docs corresponds to `FileUploadDragAndDropCustomScenarioExample.razor` (based on the file name and the fact that it shows a custom solution). Let me look at that example again:

- `Hidden="@false"` 
- `InputClass="file-upload-input"` (absolutely positioned, opacity 0, z-index 10)
- `@ondragenter="@SetDragClass"` on MudFileUpload → passed to InputFile via UserAttributes
- `@ondragleave="@ClearDragClass"` on MudFileUpload → passed to InputFile via UserAttributes, but OVERRIDDEN by `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"`

So the user's `ClearDragClass` is never called because `OnDragResetAsync` overrides it. But `OnDragResetAsync` IS called (it's the explicit handler). However, the user doesn't notice because:
1. `OnDragResetAsync` sets `_draggingState = false`
2. But `Hidden=false`, so the input doesn't change visibility
3. The user's `ClearDragClass` never runs, so `_dragClass` stays as the drag-over style

So the formatting doesn't switch back because the user's handler is overridden!

Now, for the `FileUploadCustomExample.razor` (which uses `@bind-Dragging`), the issue might be different. But the PR specifically mentions the "Create a Custom Solution" example, which is the one with `Hidden="@false"`.

So the fix needs to ensure that:
1. The user's `ondragleave` handler (from UserAttributes) is called in addition to the component's own handler
2. Or, the component should not override the user's handlers

Since Blazor doesn't support multiple handlers, we need to modify the code to call the user's handler from within our handler. But we can't easily access individual event handlers from `UserAttributes`.

Actually, looking at this differently, I think the proper fix is to remove the explicit `@ondragleave`, `@ondrop`, `@ondragend` from the `InputFile` and instead handle them in a way that doesn't conflict with user-provided handlers. But these handlers are needed for the default (non-custom) case to work.

Wait, let me look at the default case again. In the default case (DragAndDrop with button):
- Button has `@ondragenter="OnDragEnterAsync"` → sets `_draggingState = true`
- InputFile has `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"` → sets `_draggingState = false`

If we remove the explicit `@ondragleave` from InputFile, the default case would break because nothing would reset `_draggingState` to false.

But what if we keep the explicit handlers but also ensure they don't conflict with user-provided ones? The issue is that when the user provides their own `@ondragleave`, it gets overridden. The user's handler is for updating their own UI (like `_dragClass`), while the component's handler is for updating `_draggingState`.

One approach: Instead of using explicit `@ondragleave` etc. on the InputFile, we could move the drag event handling to the code-behind by using JavaScript interop or by handling it at a higher level. But that's complex.

Another approach: The `OnDragResetAsync` already sets `_draggingState = false`. If the user binds to `Dragging` or `DraggingChanged`, they'll be notified. The problem is only when the user sets their own `@ondragleave` on MudFileUpload, which gets overridden.

Actually, the simplest fix might be: The user shouldn't set `@ondragleave` on MudFileUpload at all. Instead, they should use `@bind-Dragging` or `DraggingChanged` to get notified when dragging ends. The docs example (`FileUploadDragAndDropCustomScenarioExample.razor`) should be updated to use `@bind-Dragging` instead of `@ondragleave`.

But wait, the PR description says this is a bug in v9.3.0. The example used to work and now it doesn't. So something changed.

Let me check the `Dragging` parameter documentation:

```csharp
/// <summary>
/// Indicates whether a drag operation is active.
/// </summary>
/// <remarks>
/// When <c>true</c>, the internal <see cref="InputFile"/> element is shown to capture the drop, which temporarily overrides <see cref="Hidden"/>.  When <c>false</c>, visibility follows <see cref="Hidden"/> again.  Drop-related events reset it to <c>false</c>.
/// </remarks>
[Parameter]
[Category(CategoryTypes.FileUpload.Behavior)]
public bool Dragging { get; set; }
```

And the `OnDragEnterAsync`/`OnDragResetAsync` methods:

```csharp
private async Task OnDragResetAsync()
{
    await _draggingState.SetValueAsync(false);
}

private Task OnDragEnterAsync()
{
    if (GetDisabledState())
    {
        return Task.CompletedTask;
    }

    return _draggingState.SetValueAsync(true);
}
```

So `OnDragResetAsync` sets `_draggingState` to false, which triggers `DraggingChanged`. If the user binds to `Dragging` via `@bind-Dragging`, they'll be notified. 

Now, looking at the `FileUploadDragAndDropCustomScenarioExample.razor` example, it does NOT use `@bind-Dragging`. Instead, it passes `@ondragleave` directly to MudFileUpload, which goes to InputFile via UserAttributes, but gets overridden.

I think the fix should be:
1. Add `@ondragenter` to the InputFile (already done)
2. Ensure that the component's drag event handlers don't override user-provided ones

For #2, one approach is to check if the user has provided an `ondragleave` handler in `UserAttributes`, and if so, call it from within `OnDragResetAsync`. But accessing specific event handlers from `UserAttributes` is tricky.

Actually, a simpler approach: We should change the code so that the user's event handlers (from UserAttributes) are called in addition to the component's handlers. We can do this by removing the explicit handlers from the InputFile and instead using a wrapper approach in the code-behind.

But wait, there's an even simpler approach. Let me look at this again:

The `InputFile` has `@attributes="UserAttributes"` BEFORE the explicit handlers:
```
@attributes="UserAttributes"
@ondragenter="OnDragEnterAsync"
@ondrop="OnDragResetAsync"
@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"
@ondragend="OnDragResetAsync"
```

In Blazor, when you have both `@attributes` and explicit attributes, the explicit ones take precedence. So if `UserAttributes` contains `ondragleave`, it's overridden by `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"`.

If we move `@attributes="UserAttributes"` AFTER the explicit handlers, then `UserAttributes` would override the explicit ones. But that would break the default case.

Actually, the correct fix is: we should NOT put `@ondragleave` etc. as explicit attributes on the InputFile if we also allow users to override them via UserAttributes. Instead, we should handle the drag events differently.

Let me think about the best approach...

The cleanest solution would be:
1. Remove `@ondragenter`, `@ondrop`, `@ondragleave`, `@ondragend` from the InputFile in the razor file
2. Move these event handlers to a wrapper element or handle them via JavaScript

But that's a big change. Let me think of a minimal fix.

Actually, looking at this from the user's perspective:
- The user wants `@ondragleave` on MudFileUpload to fire when dragging leaves
- Currently, it doesn't fire because the component overrides it

The minimal fix: We should ensure that the component calls the user's event handler if one is provided. We can do this by:
1. Keeping the explicit handlers on the InputFile
2. In `OnDragResetAsync` and `OnDragEnterAsync`, also invoke any user-provided handler from `UserAttributes`

Let me implement this. First, let me check how to access the user's handler from `UserAttributes`:

But actually, let me reconsider. The PR description says the issue is with v9.3.0. Maybe the issue was introduced by a recent change. Let me check if there's something specific about the `hidden` attribute or the drag events that changed.

Wait, I just realized something important. The `InputFile` has `@attributes="UserAttributes"` and then explicit `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"`. In Blazor, the explicit one wins. But what if the user doesn't set `@ondragleave` on MudFileUpload? Then `UserAttributes` doesn't contain `ondragleave`, and the explicit `OnDragResetAsync` is the only handler. That should work fine.

The issue is only when the user DOES set `@ondragleave` on MudFileUpload. In that case, their handler is overridden.

But looking at the "Create a Custom Solution" example (`FileUploadDragAndDropCustomScenarioExample.razor`), the user sets `@ondragleave="@ClearDragClass"`. This gets overridden.

Now, for the `FileUploadCustomExample.razor` (which is also a custom solution but uses `@bind-Dragging`), the user does NOT set `@ondragleave`. So the override issue doesn't apply. But the PR says this example also doesn't work.

Wait, let me re-read the PR: "Open file upload sample in the MudBlazor docs, at the Create a Custom Solution section." The "Create a Custom Solution" section in the docs might show the `FileUploadCustomExample.razor` (which uses `@bind-Dragging`), not the `FileUploadDragAndDropCustomScenarioExample.razor`.

Actually, maybe the fix is simpler than I think. Let me look at the problem from the perspective of the `FileUploadDragAndDropCustomScenarioExample.razor`:

The user sets `@ondragenter`, `@ondragleave`, `@ondragend`, `@ondrop` on `MudFileUpload`. These go to `UserAttributes`. They want these handlers to be called when the corresponding events fire on the InputFile.

The component also needs to track drag state internally. It does this via `OnDragEnterAsync` and `OnDragResetAsync`.

The issue is that `@ondragleave="OnDragResetAsync"` overrides the user's `@ondragleave` from `UserAttributes`.

**The fix**: Move `@attributes="UserAttributes"` to AFTER the explicit drag handlers. This way, the user's handlers will override the component's handlers. But then the component's internal state management would break for users who DO provide their own handlers.

But wait: users who provide their own handlers typically also use `@bind-Dragging` to manage the drag state themselves. They don't need the component's internal handlers. So overriding the component's handlers with the user's is actually the right behavior.

For users who DON'T provide their own handlers (like the default case), the component's explicit handlers would be used (since `UserAttributes` wouldn't contain those handlers).

So the fix is simply to move `@attributes="UserAttributes"` AFTER the explicit drag event handlers!
